### Killer Edge Cases
Here are 3 potential edge cases that could break a naive solution (e.g., one assuming the smallest 3 values in `b` are always the singles, or using 32-bit integers):

1. **Minimal input**: All `a_i = 1` → `b = [1, 1, 1, 2, 2, 2, 3]`. Naive "smallest 3 are singles" works here, but combined with duplicates tests multiset handling.
2. **Maximum constraint input**: `b = [300000000, 300000000, 300000000, 600000000, 600000000, 600000000, 900000000]`. Requires 64-bit integers to avoid overflow in sums (e.g., `3 * 3e8 = 9e8`).
3. **Boundary values with large single > small pair**: `a = [1, 1, 999999998]` → `b = [1, 1, 2, 999999998, 999999999, 999999999, 1000000000]`. Breaks naive "smallest 3 are singles" since `b[3] = 999999998` (single) > `b[2] = 2` (pair `1+1`).

### Plan
This plan uses brute-force enumeration of candidate singles (only `C(6,3) = 20` combinations per test case), combined with exact multiset matching. It handles **all edge cases**:
- Duplicates (minimal/all-same) via sorting/multiset check.
- Large values via 64-bit integers.
- Interleaved singles/pairs (boundary/large-single case) by trying **all** position combos and validating `sum == S` + multiset.
- Guaranteed to find a solution (per problem) in <1ms per test (`5000 * 20 * log(6) ~ 100k ops`).
- Easy to implement in any language (e.g., Python/C++).

#### Step 1: Read Input
- Read `t` (1 ≤ t ≤ 5000).
- For each test case:
  - Read 7 integers `b[0..6]` (1 ≤ b[i] ≤ 1e9, non-decreasing).
  - Let `S = b[6]` (0-based; the triple sum, always largest).

#### Step 2: Enumerate Candidate Singles
- Use three nested loops to pick **distinct positions** `i < j < k` from `0` to `5` (20 combos):
  ```
  for i in 0..4:
      for j in i+1..5:
          for k in j+1..5:
  ```
- Let candidates `x = b[i]`, `y = b[j]`, `z = b[k]` (positive by input).

#### Step 3: Validate Candidates (Quick Filters)
- Compute `candidate_sum = x + y + z` (use 64-bit: `long long` in C++, `int` in Python3).
- **If `candidate_sum != S`**: Skip (filters ~90% of invalid combos; handles large-single case where wrong picks overshoot).
- Compute pair sums: `p1 = S - x`, `p2 = S - y`, `p3 = S - z`.
- **If any `p1 < 1` or `p2 < 1` or `p3 < 1`**: Skip (ensures positive; rare, but covers `b[5] == S` hypotheticals).

#### Step 4: Multiset Check (Confirm Exact Match)
- Build list `sums = [x, y, z, p1, p2, p3]`.
- Sort `sums` (ascending).
- **If `sorted(sums) == b[0..5]`**: Valid! Output `x y z` (any order fine) and **break** (first found is OK; problem allows any).
  - Handles duplicates (e.g., minimal/all-same: matches `[1,1,1,2,2,2]`).
  - Handles interleaving (e.g., boundary: `[1,1,2,999999998,999999999,999999999]` matches).

#### Step 5: Output
- For each test case, print the 3 values separated by spaces (e.g., `1 4 3`).
- No need for sorting output (any valid `a` works).

#### Why This Handles Edge Cases
| Edge Case | How Handled |
|-----------|-------------|
| **Minimal** (`[1,1,1,2,2,2,3]`) | Picks `i=0,j=1,k=2` → sum=3==3, pairs=[2,2,2], sorted matches. Duplicates OK via sort. |
| **Maximum** (`3e8 x3, 6e8 x3, 9e8`) | 64-bit sum=9e8==S, pairs=6e8 x3, matches. No overflow. |
| **Boundary large-single** (`[1,1,2,999999998,...]`) | Picks `i=0,j=1,k=3` → sum=1e9==S, pairs=[999999999,999999999,2], sorted matches. Rejects small-3 naive pick (sum=1+1+2=4 !=1e9). |
- **All cases**: `sum==S` rejects wrong interleaves/mis-picks; multiset rejects value mismatches.

#### Implementation Notes
- **Python** (simple, no overflow):
  ```python
  import sys; input = sys.stdin.read; data = input().split()
  t = int(data[0]); idx = 1
  for _ in range(t):
      b = [int(data[idx+i]) for i in range(7)]; idx += 7; S = b[6]
      for i in range(6):
          for j in range(i+1,6):
              for k in range(j+1,6):
                  x,y,z = b[i],b[j],b[k]
                  if x+y+z == S:
                      p1,p2,p3 = S-x,S-y,S-z
                      if p1>=1 and p2>=1 and p3>=1:
                          sums = sorted([x,y,z,p1,p2,p3])
                          if sums == b[:6]: print(x,y,z); break
              else: continue; break
          else: continue; break
  ```
- **C++** (faster): Use `vector<long long> b(7);` loops same, `sort(sums.begin(), sums.end())`.
- **Time/Space**: O(1) per test; total <0.1s.
- **No false positives**: `sum==S` + pairs=other-two + multiset ensures exact generation.
- **Guaranteed hit**: Problem states ≥1 solution exists.

### Detailed Plan to Solve the Problem

#### Step 1: Understand the Problem and Core Logic
- A string `s` of length `n` is "square" **if and only if**:
  - `n` is even (since it must be exactly two identical halves).
  - The first half `s[0:n//2]` exactly equals the second half `s[n//2:n]`.
- This directly matches the definition: `s = prefix + prefix` for some `prefix` of length `n//2`.
- No other conditions (e.g., no need to check for smaller repeats or substrings).
- Output "YES" or "NO" (case-insensitive, but we'll use uppercase for simplicity).
- Constraints are small (`1 ≤ t ≤ 100`, `1 ≤ n ≤ 100`), so O(n) per test case is fine (no efficiency issues).

#### Step 2: Identify and Handle Killer Edge Cases
We'll explicitly handle these in the logic/code:
1. **Empty/minimal input (n=1)**:
   - n=1 is odd → immediately "NO".
   - Example: "a" → NO (can't split into two non-empty identical parts).
2. **Maximum constraint input (n=100)**:
   - Check if even (100 is even). Compare two strings of length 50.
   - No performance issue (string comparison is O(50)).
   - Example: 100 'a's → halves identical → "YES".
3. **Special patterns or boundary values**:
   - **All identical chars**: Even n → "YES" (e.g., "aaaa"); odd n → "NO" (e.g., "aaa").
   - **Alternating/repeating**: "xyxy" (n=4, "xy"=="xy") → "YES"; "xxyy" ("xx"!="yy") → "NO".
   - **Odd lengths**: Always "NO" (e.g., "abacaba" n=7).
   - **Minimal even**: n=2, "aa" → "YES"; "ab" → "NO".

This logic handles **all** cases from examples and edges—no naive pitfalls (e.g., no assuming halves must be minimal or checking substrings).

#### Step 3: High-Level Algorithm (Pseudocode)
```
Read t
For each of t test cases:
    Read string s
    n = length(s)
    if n % 2 != 0:
        output "NO"
    else:
        half = n // 2
        if s[0:half] == s[half:n]:
            output "YES"
        else:
            output "NO"
```

#### Step 4: Step-by-Step Implementation Plan (in Python, for clarity)
1. **Read input**:
   - Read `t = int(input())`.
   - Loop `t` times: `s = input().strip()` (strip to handle any whitespace, though not needed per constraints).

2. **Compute length**:
   - `n = len(s)` (1 ≤ n ≤ 100 guaranteed).

3. **Check parity**:
   - `if n % 2 != 0: print("NO"); continue`

4. **Split and compare halves** (only if even):
   - `half = n // 2`
   - `first = s[:half]`
   - `second = s[half:]` (in Python, `s[half:]` goes to end).
   - `if first == second: print("YES") else: print("NO")`

5. **Output formatting**:
   - One line per test case.
   - Use uppercase "YES"/"NO" (accepted in any case).

#### Step 5: Verification Against Examples and Edges
| Input | n | Even? | Halves | Equal? | Expected | Matches? |
|-------|---|-------|--------|--------|----------|----------|
| a     | 1 | No    | -      | -      | NO      | Yes     |
| aa    | 2 | Yes   | "a","a"| Yes    | YES     | Yes     |
| aaa   | 3 | No    | -      | -      | NO      | Yes     |
| aaaa  | 4 | Yes   | "aa","aa"| Yes | YES  | Yes     |
| abab  | 4 | Yes   | "ab","ab"| Yes | YES  | Yes     |
| abcabc|6 | Yes   | "abc","abc"| Yes| YES | Yes     |
| abacaba|7| No  | -      | -      | NO      | Yes     |
| xxyy  | 4 | Yes   | "xx","yy"| No  | NO      | Yes     |
| xyyx  | 4 | Yes   | "xy","yx"| No  | NO      | Yes     |
| xyxy  | 4 | Yes   | "xy","xy"| Yes | YES  | Yes     |
| **Edge: 100 'a's** |100| Yes |50 'a's each| Yes| YES| Yes|
| **Edge: "a"*99**  |99| No | -     | -     | NO      | Yes|

#### Step 6: Potential Pitfalls and Defenses
- **Off-by-one slicing**: Python slicing `s[:half]` and `s[half:]` is exact for even n.
- **Odd n**: Early exit prevents slicing errors.
- **Non-lowercase**: Constraints guarantee lowercase.
- **Leading/trailing space**: `strip()` handles if any.
- **t=1 or t=100**: Loop handles.
- **No false positives**: E.g., "abcabcabcabc" (n=12) → "abcabc"=="abcabc" → YES (correct, as it's some string twice).
- **No false negatives**: E.g., "baabaa" → "baa"=="baa" → YES.

#### Step 7: Sample Code (Ready to Copy-Paste)
```python
import sys
input = sys.stdin.read
data = input().splitlines()

t = int(data[0])
idx = 1
for _ in range(t):
    s = data[idx].strip()
    idx += 1
    n = len(s)
    if n % 2 != 0:
        print("NO")
    else:
        half = n // 2
        if s[:half] == s[half:]:
            print("YES")
        else:
            print("NO")
```
- Uses `sys.stdin.read()` for efficiency (though unnecessary for small t/n).
- Fully handles all edges.

This plan is **complete, correct, efficient, and easy to implement** (under 20 lines). No further checks needed.

### Detailed Plan to Solve the Problem

#### Overview
- **Model the Problem**: Treat the n positions (1 to n, indexed 0 to n-1 in code) as nodes in a graph. 'E' between positions i and (i+1)%n means they **must be equal** (union them into the same equivalence class/component). 'N' means they **must be unequal**.
- **Key Insight**: Use Union-Find (Disjoint Set Union - DSU) to group positions that must be equal via chains of 'E's. After processing all 'E's, check every 'N': if the two endpoints are in the **same component**, it's impossible (forced equal but required unequal). Otherwise, possible (assign same value within components, distinct values across components connected by 'N').
- **Why This Works**:
  - Handles circular nature via `(i+1) % n`.
  - Propagates equalities correctly (transitive).
  - No other constraints: infinite positive integers available (e.g., assign each component a unique value ≤ 10^9).
- **Time Complexity**: O(t * n * α(n)) = O(1000 * 50 * 5) ≈ negligible (α is inverse Ackermann, nearly constant).
- **Space**: O(n) per test case.

#### Step-by-Step Implementation Plan
1. **Read Input**:
   - Read t (1 ≤ t ≤ 1000).
   - For each test case:
     - Read string s (len(s) = n, 2 ≤ n ≤ 50, consists of 'E'/'N').

2. **Initialize Union-Find (DSU)**:
   - Create parent[0..n-1] where parent[i] = i initially.
   - Create rank[0..n-1] = 0 for union-by-rank.
   - Implement standard DSU functions:
     ```pseudocode
     find(x):
       if parent[x] != x:
         parent[x] = find(parent[x])  // path compression
       return parent[x]
     union(x, y):
       px = find(x), py = find(y)
       if px == py: return
       if rank[px] < rank[py]:
         parent[px] = py
       elif rank[px] > rank[py]:
         parent[py] = px
       else:
         parent[py] = px
         rank[px]++
     ```

3. **Process 'E' Constraints (Build Equivalence Classes)**:
   - For i from 0 to n-1:
     - If s[i] == 'E':
       - union(i, (i+1) % n)

4. **Validate 'N' Constraints**:
   - possible = true
   - For i from 0 to n-1:
     - If s[i] == 'N':
       - If find(i) == find((i+1) % n):
         - possible = false
         - break
   - Output "YES" if possible, else "NO".

5. **Output for All Test Cases**:
   - Print one line per test case.

#### Handling Killer Edge Cases
The plan explicitly handles these via the circular Union-Find model:

1. **Empty/Minimal Input (n=2)**:
   - Examples:
     | s    | Unions | 'N' Checks | Result | Reason |
     |------|--------|------------|--------|--------|
     | "EE" | 0-1 (twice) | None | YES | All equal. |
     | "EN" | 0-1 | 1 and 0 same | NO | Contradiction. |
     | "NN" | None | 0!=1, 1!=0 (different components) | YES | Assign a[0]=1, a[1]=2. |
   - Handled: n=2 uses %2 correctly; no special code needed.

2. **Maximum Constraint Input (n=50)**:
   - Worst case: t=1000, n=50 all 'E's → one component, no 'N's → YES.
   - All 'N's → n singletons, all 'N' checks pass (different components) → YES.
   - Dense unions (49 'E's +1 'N') → full component + 'N' within → NO.
   - Handled: O(n α(n)) scales fine (no performance issue); small n prevents stack overflow in recursion (path compression iterative if needed).

3. **Special Patterns / Boundary Values**:
   - **All 'E's**: One component, no 'N's → YES (e.g., all a_i=1).
   - **All 'N's (odd n, e.g., n=3 "NNN")**: No unions (all singletons), all 'N' checks pass → YES (e.g., a=[1,2,3]).
   - **Wrapping Equality + 'N' (e.g., n=3 "EEN")**: Unions connect 0-1-2 → one component; 'N' between 2-0 same → NO.
   - **Alternating "ENEN..." (even n)**: Alternating components; 'N's between different → YES.
   - **Single 'N' in sea of 'E's (n=4 "EEEN")**: Unions connect all → 'N' fails → NO.
   - **Disconnected components (e.g., "NEN")**: Unions only where 'E'; 'N's between different → YES.
   - Handled: Circular %n + post-union 'N' checks catch all propagation/wrapping issues.

#### Additional Robustness
- **No False Positives/Negatives**: Proven correct (equalities transitive, inequalities only checked post-propagation).
- **No Need for Value Assignment**: Existence only; if passes, assign component ID as value (1 to n ≤50 <1e9).
- **Code Pitfalls Avoided**:
  - Always use %n for circular.
  - Check 'N's **after** all unions (not interleaved).
  - 0-based indexing consistent.
- **Testing Recommendation**:
  - Use sample input.
  - Add: n=2 all cases; n=3 "NNN"; n=4 "EEEN"; n=50 all 'E'; n=50 all 'N'; n=50 one 'N' rest 'E's.

This plan is **easy to implement** (standard DSU + two loops) and **bulletproof** for all cases. 

#### Sample Pseudocode
```
read t
for _ in 1..t:
  read s
  n = len(s)
  parent = [0..n-1], rank=[0]*n
  for i=0..n-1:
    if s[i]=='E':
      union(i, (i+1)%n)
  possible = true
  for i=0..n-1:
    if s[i]=='N' and find(i)==find((i+1)%n):
      possible=false
      break
  print(possible ? "YES" : "NO")
```

```python
import sys

def find(parent, x):
    if parent[x] != x:
        parent[x] = find(parent, parent[x])
    return parent[x]

def union(parent, rank, x, y):
    px = find(parent, x)
    py = find(parent, y)
    if px == py:
        return
    if rank[px] < rank[py]:
        parent[px] = py
    elif rank[px] > rank[py]:
        parent[py] = px
    else:
        parent[py] = px
        rank[px] += 1

input = sys.stdin.read
data = input().splitlines()
idx = 0
t = int(data[idx])
idx += 1
for _ in range(t):
    s = data[idx]
    idx += 1
    n = len(s)
    parent = list(range(n))
    rank = [0] * n
    for i in range(n):
        if s[i] == 'E':
            union(parent, rank, i, (i + 1) % n)
    possible = True
    for i in range(n):
        if s[i] == 'N':
            if find(parent, i) == find(parent, (i + 1) % n):
                possible = False
                break
    print("YES" if possible else "NO")

### Detailed Plan to Solve the Problem

#### Step 1: Understand the Core Requirements
- We must break **exactly one** stick of length `L` into two pieces `x` and `y` where `x >= 1`, `y >= 1`, `x + y = L` (both integers).
- The resulting four lengths `{P, Q, x, y}` (where `P` and `Q` are the unbroken sticks) must form a rectangle: exactly two pairs of equal lengths (i.e., two sides of length `a` and two of length `b`, where `a` and `b` may be equal).
- This requires the multiset to have either:
  - Four equal lengths, or
  - Exactly two distinct lengths, each appearing twice.
- Constraints: `t <= 10^4`, `1 <= l_i <= 10^8` → Solution must be O(1) per testcase (no loops over splits).
- Output "YES" (case-insensitive) if possible for any choice of stick to break; else "NO".

#### Step 2: Key Insight (Derived Conditions)
After exhaustive case analysis, it is possible to break `L` (with unbroken `P`, `Q`) **if and only if**:
- **Case A**: `P == Q` **and** `L % 2 == 0` (split `L` into `L/2` and `L/2`; gives two `P` and two `L/2`).
  - Implicitly `L >= 2` (since `L >= 1` and even → `L >= 2`; `L/2 >= 1`).
- **OR**
- **Case B**: `L == P + Q` (split `L` into `P` and `Q`; gives two `P` and two `Q`).
- These cover **all** possibilities (including squares and when `P == Q` in Case B, i.e., `L = 2P`).
- Odd total sum `S = l1 + l2 + l3` is **automatically impossible** (perimeter `2(a + b) = S` can't be odd), and our conditions fail naturally if `S` odd.
- No other splits work (proven by enumerating equalities in `{P, Q, x, L-x}`).

#### Step 3: High-Level Algorithm
```
For each testcase (l1, l2, l3):
    If can_break(l1, l2, l3) OR can_break(l2, l1, l3) OR can_break(l3, l1, l2):
        Output "YES"
    Else:
        Output "NO"

def can_break(L, P, Q):
    return (P == Q and L % 2 == 0) or (L == P + Q)
```
- Try breaking each stick exactly once (3 checks, O(1)).
- Use 64-bit integers (`long long` in C++) for safety (`P + Q <= 2*10^8`).

#### Step 4: Handling Killer Edge Cases
Explicitly verify these break naive solutions (e.g., looping over splits, missing parity, or assuming `L >= 2` explicitly):

1. **Minimal/Empty Input (Boundary: All `li=1`)**:
   - Test: `1 1 1` (sum=3 odd).
   - Expected: "NO" (can't split `1`; conditions fail: odd `L`, `L != 2`).
   - Naive fail: Might loop `x=1 to L-1` (empty for `L=1`) but miss parity.
   - Our plan: All three `can_break(1,1,1)` fail (`1%2!=0`, `1!=2`).

2. **Maximum Constraint Input**:
   - Test: `100000000 100000000 100000000` (sum=300000000 even).
   - Expected: "YES" (break any; `P=Q=100000000`, `L=100000000` even).
   - Naive fail: Integer overflow on `P+Q` or slow loops (`10^8` iterations).
   - Our plan: `P==Q` and `L%2==0` (100000000 even) → passes instantly.

3. **Special Pattern/Boundary (Two minimal equal, one boundary)**:
   - Test: `1 1 2` (sum=4 even; all equal after split).
   - Expected: "YES" (break `2` → `1,1`; lengths `1,1,1,1`).
   - Also test: `1 1 3` (sum=5 odd) → "NO".
   - Naive fail: Might miss even-split when `P=Q` or assume sum check needed.
   - Our plan: For break `2`: `P=1==Q=1`, `2%2==0` → "YES". For `1 1 3`: `3%2!=0`, `3!=2` → "NO".

Additional edges auto-handled:
- Sum odd: `2 5 2` → "NO".
- `L = P + Q` max: `50000000 50000000 100000000` → "YES".
- All equal odd: `3 3 3` → "NO".
- `1 2 3` → "YES" (break `3=1+2`).

#### Step 5: Implementation Steps (Pseudocode → Real Code)
1. Read `t`.
2. For each testcase:
   - Read `long long a, b, c`.
   - Check:
     ```
     bool yes = (b == c && a % 2 == 0) || (a == b + c) ||
                (a == c && b % 2 == 0) || (b == a + c) ||
                (a == b && c % 2 == 0) || (c == a + b);
     ```
   - Print `"YES"` or `"NO"` (uppercase).
3. **Language Notes** (C++ for speed):
   - Use `fast IO`: `ios::sync_with_stdio(0); cin.tie(0);`.
   - `long long` for lengths.
   - `% 2` safe (even for `1`).
   - No sorting needed.
4. **Time/Space**: O(t) = O(10^4), trivial.

#### Step 6: Verification with Sample
| Input | Checks | Result |
|-------|--------|--------|
| `6 1 5` | Break6: `1!=5`, but `6==1+5` → YES | YES |
| `2 5 2` | Break5: `2==2` but `5%2!=0`; `5!=4`.<br>Others fail. | NO |
| `2 4 2` | Break4: `2==2`, `4%2==0` → YES | YES |
| `5 5 4` | Break4: `5==5`, `4%2==0` → YES | YES |

#### Step 7: Potential Pitfalls & Fixes
- **Overflow**: Use `long long`; `a == b + c` → `b + c` may overflow `int` (fix: `long long`).
- **L=1**: Handled (odd, can't split).
- **Even L=2, P=Q=1**: Handled.
- **P=Q, L odd**: Fails correctly.
- **Case-insensitivity**: Print fixed "YES"/"NO".
- **No explicit sum check**: Unnecessary (auto-fails).

This plan is complete, efficient, and handles all cases. Implement directly in O(1) per test.

### Detailed Plan to Solve the Problem

#### Step 0: High-Level Approach
- **Core Insight**: The robot cleans the dirty cell (r_d, c_d) at the earliest time `t >= 0` when its position (r, c) satisfies `r == r_d` **OR** `c == c_d`. Cleaning happens *before* each move (including t=0).
- **Movement Model**: Rows and columns evolve **independently** like 1D bouncing particles with velocity ±1, reflecting off walls (1 and n for rows; 1 and m for columns). Special case for size=1 (robot stays put, direction flips).
- **Solution Strategy**: Direct simulation per test case. States are finite (O(n) for rows × O(m) for cols), so it terminates quickly (max ~20,000 steps/test worst-case, total ~2×10^8 operations across 10^4 tests, safe for C++/Python).
- **No Precomputation Needed**: Simulation handles all cases uniformly.
- **Output**: For each test, the minimal `t`.

#### Step 1: Handle Input/Output Efficiently
- Read `t` (1 ≤ t ≤ 10^4).
- For each test case: Read 6 ints `n, m, r_b, c_b, r_d, c_d` (1 ≤ n,m ≤ 100, valid positions).
- Use fast I/O:
  - C++: `std::cin` with `std::ios::sync_with_stdio(false); cin.tie(NULL);`
  - Python: `sys.stdin.read()` to read all input at once.
- Output one integer per test case, newline-separated.

#### Step 2: Initialization Per Test Case
```
r = r_b
c = c_b
dr = 1  // initial down (rows increase top-to-bottom)
dc = 1  // initial right
time = 0
```

#### Step 3: Simulation Loop (Core Logic)
```
while true:
    if r == r_d or c == c_d:
        output time
        break

    // Move ROWS independently
    tent_r = r + dr
    if tent_r < 1 or tent_r > n:
        dr = -dr
        tent_r = r + dr  // recompute tentative with new dr
    if 1 <= tent_r <= n:
        r = tent_r
    // else: stay at r (only happens if n==1)

    // Move COLUMNS independently (identical logic)
    tent_c = c + dc
    if tent_c < 1 or tent_c > m:
        dc = -dc
        tent_c = c + dc
    if 1 <= tent_c <= m:
        c = tent_c
    // else: stay at c (only if m==1)

    time += 1
```
- **Why This Works**:
  - Checks cleaning **before** move (correct for t=0).
  - Reflections independent (handles corners naturally, e.g., both reflect if hitting corner).
  - For n≥2/m≥2: `tent_*` after reflect always in bounds.
  - For n=1: Always reflects and `tent_r` out → stays, `dr` flips (irrelevant for position).
  - Guaranteed termination (problem states "always cleans eventually").

#### Step 4: Verification Against Examples
- **Example 1** (10x10, (6,1)→(2,8)): Simulates to t=7 at (7,8), `c=8==8` → correct.
- **Example 5** (2x2, (1,1)→(2,1)): t=0, `c=1==1` → correct.
- Matches all provided outputs/images.

#### Step 5: Handling Killer Edge Cases Explicitly
The plan inherently handles these via the stay/reflect logic and simulation:

1. **Empty/Minimal Input (n=1, m=1; n=1 m>1; m=1 n>1)**:
   - n=1: Row stays at 1 forever (`tent_r` always out → stay). Cleans if `r_d=1` (always true) at t=0.
   - m=1: Col stays at 1. Cleans if `c_d=1` at t=0.
   - n=m=1: t=0 always (same position).
   - Test: n=1 m=2 (1,1)→(1,2): t=0 (`r=1==1`).

2. **Maximum Constraint Input (n=100, m=100)**:
   - Worst-case steps: ~lcm(2*n, 2*m) ≤ ~20,000 (row period ~2n, col ~2m).
   - Total ops: 10^4 tests × 2×10^4 = 2×10^8 → <1s in C++.
   - No TLE: Loop is tight (simple arithmetic, no arrays/conditionals beyond ifs).

3. **Special Patterns/Boundary Values**:
   - **t=0 cases**: Initial share row/col (e.g., last example; robot on dirt).
   - **Corners**: (1,1) dr=1 dc=1 → (2,2) if n,m≥2; both reflect at (n,m).
   - **Parity issues**: Even/odd n (e.g., n=2 oscillates 1↔2; n=3 visits all).
   - **Dirt opposite corner**: Sim visits shared row/col within period.
   - Test: n=2 m=2 (1,1)→(2,2): t=1 (`r=2==2`).

#### Step 6: Implementation Guidelines
- **Language**: C++ for speed (Python ok if using pypy).
- **Pseudocode to C++**:
  ```cpp
  #include <bits/stdc++.h>
  using namespace std;
  int main() {
      ios::sync_with_stdio(false); cin.tie(NULL);
      int t; cin >> t;
      for(int test=0; test<t; test++) {
          int n,m,rb,cb,rd,cd; cin>>n>>m>>rb>>cb>>rd>>cd;
          int r=rb, c=cb, dr=1, dc=1, time=0;
          while(true) {
              if(r==rd || c==cd) {
                  cout << time << '\n';
                  break;
              }
              // row move
              int tr = r + dr;
              if(tr < 1 || tr > n) {
                  dr = -dr;
                  tr = r + dr;
              }
              if(tr >=1 && tr <=n) r = tr;
              // col move
              int tc = c + dc;
              if(tc < 1 || tc > m) {
                  dc = -dc;
                  tc = c + dc;
              }
              if(tc >=1 && tc <=m) c = tc;
              time++;
          }
      }
  }
  ```
- **No infinite loop safeguard needed** (guaranteed), but add `assert(time < 100000)` if paranoid.
- **Debug**: Log positions for first example.

#### Step 7: Optimizations (Optional, Not Needed)
- Precompute row sequence until repeats (O(n) states), find min t with row[t]==rd; same for col; take min over union.
- But simulation simpler/faster in practice.

#### Step 8: Testing Plan
- **Unit Tests**:
  - All 5 samples.
  - n=1 m=1 (1,1)→(1,1): 0.
  - n=1 m=100 (1,1)→(1,100): 0.
  - n=100 m=100 (1,1)→(100,100): Simulate manually (~199 steps?).
  - n=2 m=2 (1,1)→(2,2): 1.
- **Stress**: 10^4 tests at max n/m, random positions → verify no TLE.

This plan is **complete, correct, efficient, and easy to implement** (copy-paste ready). Handles all edges without special cases beyond the unified move logic.

```python
import sys

data = sys.stdin.read().split()
idx = 0
t = int(data[idx])
idx += 1

for _ in range(t):
    n = int(data[idx])
    m = int(data[idx + 1])
    rb = int(data[idx + 2])
    cb = int(data[idx + 3])
    rd = int(data[idx + 4])
    cd = int(data[idx + 5])
    idx += 6
    
    r = rb
    c = cb
    dr = 1
    dc = 1
    time = 0
    
    while True:
        if r == rd or c == cd:
            print(time)
            break
        
        # move row
        tr = r + dr
        if tr < 1 or tr > n:
            dr = -dr
            tr = r + dr
        if 1 <= tr <= n:
            r = tr
        
        # move col
        tc = c + dc
        if tc < 1 or tc > m:
            dc = -dc
            tc = c + dc
        if 1 <= tc <= m:
            c = tc
        
        time += 1
```
